## Your Task

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

     1→package identity

     3→import (
     4→	"fmt"

     6→)
     7→
     8→// swagger:enum RoleType
     9→type RoleType string
    10→
    11→const (
    12→	RoleNone   RoleType = "None"
    13→	RoleViewer RoleType = "Viewer"
    14→	RoleEditor RoleType = "Editor"
    15→	RoleAdmin  RoleType = "Admin"
    16→)
    17→
    18→var rolePrecedence = map[RoleType]int{
    19→	RoleNone:   10,
    20→	RoleViewer: 20,
    21→	RoleEditor: 30,
    22→	RoleAdmin:  40,
    23→}
    24→
    25→// Needed to keep stable order
    26→var roleOrder = [...]RoleType{
    27→	RoleNone,
    28→	RoleViewer,
    29→	RoleEditor,
    30→	RoleAdmin,
    31→}
    32→
    33→func (r RoleType) IsValid() bool {
    34→	_, ok := rolePrecedence[r]
    35→	return ok
    36→}
    37→
    38→func (r RoleType) Includes(other RoleType) bool {
    39→	return rolePrecedence[r] >= rolePrecedence[other]
    40→}
    41→
    42→func (r RoleType) Children() []RoleType {
    43→	children := make([]RoleType, 0, 3)
    44→
    45→	for _, role := range roleOrder {
    46→		if rolePrecedence[r] > rolePrecedence[role] {
    47→			children = append(children, role)
    48→		}
    49→	}
    50→
    51→	return children
    52→}
    53→
    54→func (r RoleType) Parents() []RoleType {
    55→	parents := make([]RoleType, 0, 3)
    56→
    57→	for _, role := range roleOrder {
    58→		if rolePrecedence[r] < rolePrecedence[role] {
    59→			parents = append(parents, role)
    60→		}
    61→	}
    62→
    63→	return parents
    64→}
    65→
    66→func (r *RoleType) UnmarshalText(data []byte) error {
    67→	// make sure "viewer" and "Viewer" are both correct
    68→	str := strings.Title(string(data))
    69→
    70→	*r = RoleType(str)
    71→	if !r.IsValid() {
    72→		if (*r) != "" {
    73→			re

    14→// ResourceResolver is called before authorization is performed.
    15→// It can be used to translate resoruce name into one or more valid scopes that
    16→// will be used for authorization. If more than one scope is returned from a resolver
    17→// only one needs to match to allow call to be authorized.
    18→type ResourceResolver interface {
    19→	Resolve(ctx context.Context, ns claims.NamespaceInfo, name string) ([]string, error)
    20→}
    21→
    22→// ResourceResolverFunc is an adapter so that functions can implement ResourceResolver.
    23→type ResourceResolverFunc func(ctx context.Context, ns claims.NamespaceInfo, name string) ([]string, error)
    24→
    25→func (r ResourceResolverFunc) Resolve(ctx context.Context, ns claims.NamespaceInfo, name string) ([]string, error) {
    26→	return r(ctx, ns, name)
    27→}
    28→
    29→type ResourceAuthorizerOptions struct {
    30→	// Resource is the resource name in plural.
    31→	Resource string
    32→	// Unchecked is used to skip authorization checks for specified verbs.
    33→	// This takes precedence over configured Mapping
    34→	Unchecked map[string]bool
    35→	// Attr is attribute used for resource scope. It's usually 'id' or 'uid'
    36→	// depending on what is stored for the resource.
    37→	Attr string
    38→	// Mapping is used to translate k8s verb to rbac action.
    39→	// Key is the desired verb and value the rbac action it should be translated into.
    40→	// If no mapping 
... (truncated)

    17→func (p PermissionType) String() string {
    18→	names := map[int]string{
    19→		int(PERMISSION_VIEW):  "View",
    20→		int(PERMISSION_EDIT):  "Edit",
    21→		int(PERMISSION_ADMIN): "Admin",
    22→	}

    24→}

    34→)

     1→package accesscontrol
     2→
     3→import (
     4→	"github.com/grafana/grafana/pkg/apimachinery/identity"
     5→)
     6→
     7→func Checker(user identity.Requester, action string) func(scopes ...string) bool {
     8→	permissions := user.GetPermissions()
     9→	userScopes, ok := permissions[action]
    10→	if !ok {
    11→		return func(scopes ...string) bool { return false }
    12→	}
    13→
    14→	lookup := make(map[string]bool, len(userScopes))
    15→	for i := range userScopes {
    16→		lookup[userScopes[i]] = true
    17→	}
    18→
    19→	var checkedWildcards bool
    20→	var hasWildcard bool
    21→
    22→	return func(scopes ...string) bool {
    23→		if !checkedWildcards {
    24→			wildcards := wildcardsFromScopes(scopes...)
    25→			for _, w := range wildcards {
    26→				if _, ok := lookup[w]; ok {
    27→					hasWildcard = true
    28→					break
    29→				}
    30→			}
    31→			checkedWildcards = true
    32→		}
    33→
    34→		if hasWildcard {
    35→			return true
    36→		}
    37→
    38→		for _, s := range scopes {
    39→			if lookup[s] {
    40→				return true
    41→			}
    42→		}
    43→		return false
    44→	}
    45→}
    46→
    47→func wildcardsFromScopes(scopes ...string) Wildcards {
    48→	prefixes := make([]string, len(scopes))
    49→	for _, scope := range scopes {
    50→		prefixes = append(prefixes, ScopePrefix(scope))
    51→	}
    52→
    53→	return WildcardsFromPrefixes(prefixes)
    54→}
    55→

   343→// GetOrgRoles returns legacy org roles for a user

   357→
   358→// PermissionsForActions generate Permissions for all actions provided scoped to provided scope.
   359→func PermissionsForActions(actions []string, scope string) []Permission {
   360→	permissions := make([]Permission, len(actions))
   361→
   362→	for i, action := range actions {
   363→		permissions[i] = Permission{
   364→			Action: action,
   365→			Scope:  scope,
   366→		}
   367→	}
   368→
   369→	return permissions
   370→}
   371→
   372→func BackgroundUser(name string, orgID int64, role org.RoleType, permissions []Permission) identity.Requester {
   373→	return &user.SignedInUser{
   374→		OrgID:   orgID,
   375→		OrgRole: role,
   376→		Login:   "grafana_" + name,
   377→		Permissions: map[int64]map[string][]string{
   378→			orgID: GroupScopesByAction(permissions),
   379→		},
   380→	}
   381→}
   382→

## Summary

I've completed a comprehensive audit of the Grafana permission model implementation and created `/workspace/answer.json` with the findings. Here's what was discovered:

### **Three-Tier Permission Model Coverage:**

**20 Key Files** implementing the three-tier system:
- **Role Definition**: `pkg/apimachinery/identity/role_type.go` (RoleViewer, RoleEditor, RoleAdmin with precedence hierarchy)
- **Permission Enforcement Middleware**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go` and `pkg/middleware/auth.go`
- **Permission Mapping**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` and `folder.go` 
- **Dashboard/Folder Management**: APIs in `pkg/api/dashboard_permission.go`, `pkg/api/folder_permission.go`
- **Inheritance System**: `apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/folder_reconciler.go`

### **Key Architecture Components:**

1. **Role Hierarchy**: Implemented via role precedence values (Viewer=20, Editor=30, Admin=40) with `Includes()` method determining which permissions each role grants

2. **Permission Levels**:
   - **Viewer**: Read-only access (PERMISSION_VIEW)
   - **Editor**: Read + Write + Delete (PERMISSION_EDIT)
   - **Admin**: Full control including permissions management (PERMISSION_ADMIN)

3. **Permission Guard Flow**:
   - User role → `GetOrgRoles()` → lookup in basic role definitions → `GetUserPermissions()` → middleware authorization → access control decision

4. **Folder/Dashboard Inheritance**: Parent folder permissions inherited by nested dashboards through `InheritedScopesSolver` functions and the `FolderReconciler` which reconciles the hierarchy

The answer includes 27 key symbols and a 7-function call chain showing the complete permission enforcement pipeline.

The roles are mirrored in `pkg/services/org/model.go` for backward compatibility.\\n\\n## Role-to-Permission Mapping\\nThe basic role definitions are created in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` via the BuildBasicRoleDefinitions() function, which returns a map of RoleType strings to RoleDTO objects. The middleware calls authorize() which evaluates whether the user has required permissions\\n\\n3. **Permission Evaluation**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/service.go` implements GetUserPermissions() and getUserPermissions(), which retrieve permissions by looking up the user's org roles (via GetOrgRoles in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`) and retrieving the mapped permissions from the basic role definitions\\n\\n4. **Role Checking**: `pkg/apimachinery/identity/static.go` implements HasRole() on the Requester interface, which checks if the user's OrgRole.Includes() the requested role. Grafana Admins always return true\\n\\n## Dashboard/Folder Inheritance\\nDashboard and folder permissions are managed through:\\n\\n1. **Dashboard Permissions API**: `pkg/api/dashboard_permission.go` provides endpoints to get and update dashboard permissions using the dashboardPermissionMap that translates \\\"View\\\", \\\"Edit\\\", \\\"Admin\\\" to PERMISSION_VIEW, PERMISSION_EDIT, PERMISSION_ADMIN values\\n\\n2. **Folder Permissions API**: `pkg/api/folder_permission.go` provides similar endpoints for folder permissions\\n\\n3. **Permission Levels**: `pkg/services/dashboards/dashboardaccess/dashboard_access.go` defines the three permission types as bitwise flags: PERMISSION_VIEW (1), PERMISSION_EDIT (2), PERMISSION_ADMIN (4)\\n\\n4. **Permission Inheritance**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` includes an InheritedScopesSolver that determines inherited permissions by looking up dashboard.FolderUID and calling GetInheritedScopes(). A precedence map (rolePrecedence) assigns numeric levels to each role (10, 20, 30, 40 respectively), and the Includes() method determines role hierarchy\u2014Admin includes Editor and Viewer, Editor includes Viewer. The roles are mirrored in `pkg/services/org/model.go` for backward compatibility.\\n\\n## Role-to-Permission Mapping\\nThe basic role definitions are created in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/roles.go` via the BuildBasicRoleDefinitions() function, which returns a map of RoleType strings to RoleDTO objects. These basic roles are initialized with empty permission arrays.\\n\\nThe actual permission assignments for Viewer/Editor/Admin roles are performed in:\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go`: registerDashboardRoles() maps Viewer \u2192 read, Editor \u2192 read+write+delete, Admin \u2192 read+write+delete+permissions\\n- `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go`: registerFolderRoles() applies similar permissions for folders, plus additional folder-specific actions\\n\\nThese permissions are granted to built-in roles through RoleRegistration objects with Grants fields that map to organization role strings.\\n\\n## Permission Guard Middleware\\nThe permission enforcement occurs through the middleware chain:\\n\\n1. **Request Authentication**: `pkg/middleware/auth.go` provides basic authentication middleware that validates user credentials\\n\\n2. **Access Control Middleware**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/middleware.go` contains the Middleware() function which wraps an Evaluator. The middleware calls authorize() which evaluates whether the user has required permissions\\n\\n3. **Permission Evaluation**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/acimpl/service.go` implements GetUserPermissions() and getUserPermissions(), which retrieve permissions by looking up the user's org roles (via GetOrgRoles in `pkg/services/accesscontrol/accesscontrol.go`) and retrieving the mapped permissions from the basic role definitions\\n\\n4. **Role Checking**: `pkg/apimachinery/identity/static.go` implements HasRole() on the Requester interface, which checks if the user's OrgRole.Includes() the requested role. Grafana Admins always return true\\n\\n## Dashboard/Folder Inheritance\\nDashboard and folder permissions are managed through:\\n\\n1. **Dashboard Permissions API**: `pkg/api/dashboard_permission.go` provides endpoints to get and update dashboard permissions using the dashboardPermissionMap that translates \\\"View\\\", \\\"Edit\\\", \\\"Admin\\\" to PERMISSION_VIEW, PERMISSION_EDIT, PERMISSION_ADMIN values\\n\\n2. **Folder Permissions API**: `pkg/api/folder_permission.go` provides similar endpoints for folder permissions\\n\\n3. **Permission Levels**: `pkg/services/dashboards/dashboardaccess/dashboard_access.go` defines the three permission types as bitwise flags: PERMISSION_VIEW (1), PERMISSION_EDIT (2), PERMISSION_ADMIN (4)\\n\\n4. **Permission Inheritance**: `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/dashboard.go` includes an InheritedScopesSolver that determines inherited permissions by looking up dashboard.FolderUID and calling GetInheritedScopes(). Similarly, `pkg/services/accesscontrol/ossaccesscontrol/folder.go` has an InheritedScopesSolver for folder parent permissions\\n\\n5. **Folder Hierarchy Reconciliation**: `apps/iam/pkg/reconcilers/folder_reconciler.go` implements the FolderReconciler which reconciles folder parent relationships and updates permission inheritance when folders are created, updated, or deleted\\n\\n## Client-Side Permission Display\\nThe frontend receives permission information through:\\n- `apps/dashboard/pkg/apis/dashboard/types.go`: DashboardAccess struct with boolean flags (CanSave, CanEdit, CanAdmin)\\n- `pkg/api/dashboard.go`: Sets these flags by evaluating user permissions using AccessControl.Evaluate()\\n- `pkg/api/dtos/acl.go`: UpdateDashboardACLCommand structures for permission management\\n\\nThe complete flow: user role \u2192 GetOrgRoles \u2192 permission lookup from basic role definitions \u2192 middleware authorization checks \u2192 access allowed/denied with appropriate permission level (View/Edit/Admin).\"\n}\n",
